       <li><a href="/wiki/Private_University_in_the_Principality_of_Liechtenstein" title="Private University in the Principality of Liechtenstein">Private University in the Principality of Liechtenstein</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_Institute" title="Liechtenstein Institute">Liechtenstein Institute</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Academy_of_Philosophy,_Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Academy of Philosophy, Liechtenstein (page does not exist)">International Academy of Philosophy, Liechtenstein</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>There are nine public high schools in the country. These include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Liechtensteinisches_Gymnasium" title="Liechtensteinisches Gymnasium">Liechtensteinisches Gymnasium</a> in Vaduz.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschule</a> Vaduz and <a href="/wiki/Oberschule" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberschule">Oberschule</a> Vaduz, in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Schulzentrum_M%C3%BChleholz_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Schulzentrum Mühleholz II (page does not exist)">Schulzentrum Mühleholz II</a> in Vaduz<sup id="cite_ref-WeiterSchaan_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeiterSchaan-69">[69]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Realschule Schaan and Sportschule Liechtenstein in <a href="/wiki/Schaan" title="Schaan">Schaan</a><sup id="cite_ref-WeiterSchaan_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeiterSchaan-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg/220px-Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg/330px-Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg/440px-Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3962" data-file-height="2597"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hubschrauberlandeplatz_Balzers_Liechtenstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Balzers_Heliport" class="mw-redirect" title="Balzers Heliport">Balzers Heliport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are about 250&nbsp;km (155 miles) of paved roadway within Liechtenstein, with 90&nbsp;km (56 miles) of marked bicycle paths. </p>
      <p>A 9.5&nbsp;km (5.9&nbsp;mi) railway connects Austria and Switzerland through Liechtenstein. The <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Liechtenstein" title="Rail transport in Liechtenstein">country's railways</a> are administered by the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Federal_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Austrian Federal Railways">Austrian Federal Railways</a> as part of the route between <a href="/wiki/Feldkirch,_Vorarlberg" title="Feldkirch, Vorarlberg">Feldkirch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buchs,_St._Gallen" title="Buchs, St. Gallen">Buchs</a>, Switzerland. Liechtenstein is nominally within the Austrian Verkehrsverbund Vorarlberg<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> tariff region. </p>
      <p>There are four railway stations in Liechtenstein, namely <a href="/wiki/Schaan-Vaduz_railway_station" title="Schaan-Vaduz railway station">Schaan-Vaduz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forst_Hilti_railway_station" title="Forst Hilti railway station">Forst Hilti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nendeln_railway_station" title="Nendeln railway station">Nendeln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schaanwald_railway_station" title="Schaanwald railway station">Schaanwald</a>, served by an irregularly stopping train service between Feldkirch and Buchs provided by <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Federal_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Austrian Federal Railways">Austrian Federal Railways</a>. While <a href="/wiki/EuroCity" title="EuroCity">EuroCity</a> and other long-distance international trains also travel along the route, they do not normally call at the stations within the borders of Liechtenstein. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_Bus" title="Liechtenstein Bus">Liechtenstein Bus</a> is a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/PostBus_Switzerland" title="PostBus Switzerland">Swiss Postbus system</a>, but separately run, and connects to the Swiss bus network at <a href="/wiki/Buchs,_St._Gallen" title="Buchs, St. Gallen">Buchs</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Sargans" title="Sargans">Sargans</a>. Buses also run to the Austrian town of Feldkirch. </p>
      <p>Liechtenstein is one of only a few <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_without_an_airport" title="List of countries without an airport">countries without an airport</a>. The nearest large airport is <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> near <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (130&nbsp;km or 80 miles by road). The nearest small airport is <a href="/wiki/St._Gallen-Altenrhein_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Gallen-Altenrhein Airport">St. Gallen Airport</a> (50&nbsp;km or 30 miles). <a href="/wiki/Friedrichshafen_Airport" title="Friedrichshafen Airport">Friedrichshafen Airport</a> also provides access to Liechtenstein, as it is 85&nbsp;km (53 miles) away. <a href="/wiki/Balzers_Heliport" class="mw-redirect" title="Balzers Heliport">Balzers Heliport</a> is<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> available for chartered helicopter flights. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Liechtenstein" title="Music of Liechtenstein">Music of Liechtenstein</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tleft">

        <a href="/wiki/File:KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg/220px-KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg/330px-KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg/440px-KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1469"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KML_HAF_aussen_vom_Staedtle_Barbara_Buehler.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kunstmuseum (<a href="/wiki/Kunstmuseum_Liechtenstein" title="Kunstmuseum Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein Art Museum</a>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum,_2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum%2C_2014.JPG/220px-Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum%2C_2014.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum%2C_2014.JPG/330px-Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum%2C_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum%2C_2014.JPG/440px-Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum%2C_2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3225" data-file-height="2151"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Liechtensteinisches_Landesmuseum,_2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_National_Museum" title="Liechtenstein National Museum">Liechtenstein National Museum</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As a result of its small size, Liechtenstein has been strongly affected by external cultural influences, most notably those originating in the southern regions of German-speaking Europe, including Austria, Baden-Wurttemberg, Bavaria, Switzerland, and specifically <a href="/wiki/German_Tyrol" title="German Tyrol">Tirol</a> and Vorarlberg. The "Historical Society of the Principality of Liechtenstein" plays a role in preserving the culture and history of the country. </p>
      <p>The largest museum is the <a href="/wiki/Kunstmuseum_Liechtenstein" title="Kunstmuseum Liechtenstein">Kunstmuseum Liechtenstein</a>, an international museum of modern and contemporary art with an important international art collection. The building by the Swiss architects Morger, Degelo, and Kerez is a landmark in Vaduz. It was completed in November 2000 and forms a "black box" of tinted concrete and black basalt stone. The museum collection is also the national art collection of Liechtenstein. </p>
      <p>The other important museum is the <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_National_Museum" title="Liechtenstein National Museum">Liechtenstein National Museum</a> (<i>Liechtensteinisches Landesmuseum</i>) showing permanent exhibition on the cultural and natural history of Liechtenstein as well as special exhibitions. There is also a stamp museum, ski museum, and a 500-year-old Rural Lifestyle Museum. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_State_Library" title="Liechtenstein State Library">Liechtenstein State Library</a> is the library that has <a href="/wiki/Legal_deposit" title="Legal deposit">legal deposit</a> for all books published in the country. </p>
      <p>The most famous historical sites are <a href="/wiki/Vaduz_Castle" title="Vaduz Castle">Vaduz Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gutenberg_Castle" title="Gutenberg Castle">Gutenberg Castle</a>, the Red House and the ruins of Schellenberg. </p>
      <p>The Private Art Collection of the Prince of Liechtenstein, one of the world's leading private art collections, is shown at the <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_Museum" title="Liechtenstein Museum">Liechtenstein Museum</a> in Vienna. </p>
      <p>On the country's national holiday all subjects are invited to the castle of the head of state. A significant portion of the population attends the national celebration at the castle where speeches are made and complimentary beer is served.<sup id="cite_ref-Letzing_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Letzing-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Music and theatre are an important part of the culture. There are numerous music organizations such as the Liechtenstein Musical Company, the annual Guitar Days, and the International Josef Gabriel Rheinberger Society, which play in two main theatres. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The primary <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service provider</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_network_operator" title="Mobile network operator">mobile network operator</a> of Liechtenstein is Telecom Liechtenstein, located in Schaan. </p>
      <p>There are two conventional television channels in the country. The private channel <a href="/wiki/1FLTV" class="mw-redirect" title="1FLTV">1FLTV</a> was created in 2008 with a goal of joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a>, which it has not accomplished yet. The <i>Landeskanal</i> (<small><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landeskanal" class="extiw" title="de:Landeskanal">de</a></small>) is operated by the government's Unit for Information and Communication and carries government proceedings, <a href="/wiki/Public_affairs_(broadcasting)" title="Public affairs (broadcasting)">public affairs</a> programming, and cultural events. Both are seen on local cable providers, along with channels from the other German-speaking countries. The only free television is <a href="/wiki/ORF_(broadcaster)" title="ORF (broadcaster)">ORF</a> from Austria, available via terrestrial overspill of its signal from <a href="/wiki/Vorarlberg" title="Vorarlberg">Vorarlberg</a>. </p>
      <p>Radio Liechtenstein (<small><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Liechtenstein" class="extiw" title="de:Radio Liechtenstein">de</a></small>), which was established in 2004 along with the public-service broadcaster <i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liechtensteinischer_Rundfunk" class="extiw" title="de:Liechtensteinischer Rundfunk">Liechtensteinischer Rundfunk</a></i> (LRF) that operates it, is the country's only domestic radio station based in Triesen. Radio Liechtenstein and several programs of the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Schweizer_Radio_und_Fernsehen" title="Schweizer Radio und Fernsehen">SRF</a> are broadcast from the Sender Erbi (<small><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sender_Erbi" class="extiw" title="de:Sender Erbi">de</a></small>) overlooking Vaduz. Liechtenstein also has two major newspapers: <i><a href="/wiki/Liechtensteiner_Volksblatt" title="Liechtensteiner Volksblatt">Liechtensteiner Volksblatt</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Liechtensteiner_Vaterland" title="Liechtensteiner Vaterland">Liechtensteiner Vaterland</a></i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">Amateur radio</a> is a hobby of some nationals and visitors. However, unlike virtually every other sovereign nation, Liechtenstein does not have its own <a href="/wiki/ITU_prefix" title="ITU prefix">ITU prefix</a>. Conventionally, amateurs are issued call signs with the Swiss prefix "HB", followed by "0" or "L". </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg/170px-Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg/255px-Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg/340px-Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2208"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Marco_B%C3%BCchel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Marco_B%C3%BCchel" title="Marco Büchel">Marco Büchel</a>, the first Liechtensteiner alpine skier to compete at six <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Liechtenstein <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> teams play in the Swiss football leagues. The <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_Football_Cup" title="Liechtenstein Football Cup">Liechtenstein Football Cup</a> allows access for one Liechtenstein team each year to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>; <a href="/wiki/FC_Vaduz" title="FC Vaduz">FC Vaduz</a>, a team playing in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Super_League" title="Swiss Super League">Swiss Super League</a>, the first division in Swiss football, is the most successful team in the Cup, and scored their greatest success in the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1996–97 UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup in 1996</a> when they drew with and defeated the Latvian team <a href="/wiki/FK_Jelgava" title="FK Jelgava">FC Universitate Riga</a> by 1–1 and 4–2, to go on to a lucrative fixture against <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain F.C.</a>, which they lost 0–3 and 0–4. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_national_football_team" title="Liechtenstein national football team">Liechtenstein national football team</a> is regarded as an easy target for any team drawn against them; this was the basis for a book about Liechtenstein's unsuccessful qualifying campaign for the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 World Cup</a> by British author <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Connelly" title="Charlie Connelly">Charlie Connelly</a>. In one surprising week during autumn 2004, however, the team managed a 2–2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a>, who only a few months earlier had been the losing finalists in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">European Championships</a>. Four days later, the Liechtenstein team traveled to Luxembourg, where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">the home team</a> 4–0 in a <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> qualifying match. In the qualification stage of the European Championship 2008, Liechtenstein beat Latvia 1–0, a result which prompted the resignation of the Latvian coach. They went on to beat Iceland 3–0 on 17 October 2007, which is considered one of the most dramatic losses of the Icelandic national football team. On 7 September 2010, they came within seconds of a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> in Glasgow, having led 1–0 earlier in the second half, but Liechtenstein lost 2–1 thanks to a goal by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_McManus" title="Stephen McManus">Stephen McManus</a> in the 97th minute. On 3 June 2011, Liechtenstein defeated <a href="/wiki/Lithuania_national_football_team" title="Lithuania national football team">Lithuania</a> 2–0. On 15 November 2014, Liechtenstein defeated <a href="/wiki/Moldova_national_football_team" title="Moldova national football team">Moldova</a> 0–1 with <a href="/wiki/Franz_Burgmeier" title="Franz Burgmeier">Franz Burgmeier</a>'s late free kick goal in <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Chișinău</a>. </p>
      <p>As an <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">alpine</a> country, the main sporting opportunity for Liechtensteiners to excel is in winter sports such as <a href="/wiki/Downhill_(ski_competition)" title="Downhill (ski competition)">downhill skiing</a>: the country's single ski area is <a href="/wiki/Malbun" title="Malbun">Malbun</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hanni_Wenzel" title="Hanni Wenzel">Hanni Wenzel</a> won two gold medals and one silver medal in the 1980 <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a> (she won bronze in 1976), her brother <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Wenzel" title="Andreas Wenzel">Andreas</a> won one silver medal in 1980 and one bronze medal in 1984 in the <a href="/wiki/Giant_slalom_skiing" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant slalom skiing">giant slalom</a> event, and her daughter <a href="/wiki/Tina_Weirather" title="Tina Weirather">Tina Weirather</a> won a bronze medal in 2018 in the <a href="/wiki/Super-G" title="Super-G">Super-G</a>. With ten medals overall (all in alpine skiing), Liechtenstein has won more Olympic medals per capita than any other nation.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> It is the smallest nation to win a medal in any Olympics, Winter or Summer, and currently the only nation to win a medal in the Winter Games but not in the Summer Games. Other notable skiers from Liechtenstein are <a href="/wiki/Marco_B%C3%BCchel" title="Marco Büchel">Marco Büchel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willi_Frommelt" title="Willi Frommelt">Willi Frommelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Frommelt" title="Paul Frommelt">Paul Frommelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ursula_Konzett" title="Ursula Konzett">Ursula Konzett</a>. </p>
      <p>Another discipline unusually popular with Liechtensteiners is <a href="/wiki/Auto_racing" title="Auto racing">motorsport</a> – American-born German-Colombian <a href="/wiki/Rikky_von_Opel" title="Rikky von Opel">Rikky von Opel</a> raced under the flag of Liechtenstein in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> in <a href="/wiki/1973_Formula_One_season" title="1973 Formula One season">1973</a> and <a href="/wiki/1974_Formula_One_season" title="1974 Formula One season">1974</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manfred_Schurti" title="Manfred Schurti">Manfred Schurti</a> competed in 9 editions of the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> factory driver with a best finish of 4th outright in <a href="/wiki/1976_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="1976 24 Hours of Le Mans">1976</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The nation is currently represented internationally by <a href="/wiki/Fabienne_Wohlwend" title="Fabienne Wohlwend">Fabienne Wohlwend</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Challenge" title="Ferrari Challenge">Ferrari Challenge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Formula_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula 3">Formula 3</a>, as well as Matthias Kaiser who competes in prototype <a href="/wiki/Endurance_racing_(motorsport)" title="Endurance racing (motorsport)">endurance racing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other sports Liechtenstein athletes have had success in include <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Vogt" title="Stephanie Vogt">Stephanie Vogt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kathinka_von_Deichmann" title="Kathinka von Deichmann">Kathinka von Deichmann</a> both having varying degrees of success on the women's tour, as well as <a href="/wiki/Swimming" title="Swimming">swimming</a> – both <a href="/wiki/Julia_Hassler" title="Julia Hassler">Julia Hassler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Meier" title="Christoph Meier">Christoph Meier</a> represented the country at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> with the former the nations' flag bearer.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Youth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_national_football_team" title="Liechtenstein national football team">Liechtenstein</a> competes in the Switzerland U16 Cup Tournament, which offers young players an opportunity to play against top football clubs. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_and_defense">Security and defense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Security and defense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Liechtenstein" class="mw-redirect" title="Law enforcement in Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein National Police</a> is responsible for keeping order within the country. It consists of 87 field officers and 38 civilian staff, totaling 125 employees. All officers are equipped with <a href="/wiki/Small_arms" class="mw-redirect" title="Small arms">small arms</a>. The country has one of the world's lowest <a href="/wiki/Crime_statistics" title="Crime statistics">crime rates</a>. Liechtenstein's prison holds few, if any, inmates, and those with sentences over two years are transferred to <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Austria" title="Judiciary of Austria">Austrian jurisdiction</a>. The Liechtenstein National Police maintains a trilateral treaty with Austria and Switzerland that enables close cross-border cooperation among the police forces of the three countries.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_(Verkehrsinstruktion).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_%28Verkehrsinstruktion%29.jpg/300px-Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_%28Verkehrsinstruktion%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_%28Verkehrsinstruktion%29.jpg/450px-Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_%28Verkehrsinstruktion%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_%28Verkehrsinstruktion%29.jpg/600px-Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_%28Verkehrsinstruktion%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2777" data-file-height="2242"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Liechtenstein_Police_traffic_instructor_(Verkehrsinstruktion).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Liechtenstein Police
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Liechtenstein follows a policy of <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutrality</a> and is one of the few <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_without_armed_forces" title="List of countries without armed forces">countries in the world that maintain no military</a>. The army was abolished soon after the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Prussian_War_of_1866" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Prussian War of 1866">Austro-Prussian War of 1866</a>, in which Liechtenstein fielded an army of 80 men, although they were not involved in any fighting. No casualties were incurred; in fact, the unit numbered 81 upon return due to an Austrian military liaison who accompanied the army back home.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The demise of the <a href="/wiki/German_Confederation" title="German Confederation">German Confederation</a> in that war freed Liechtenstein from its international obligation to maintain an army, and parliament seized this opportunity and refused to provide funding for one. The Prince objected, as such a move would leave the country defenceless, but relented on 12 February 1868 and disbanded the force. The last soldier to serve under the colours of Liechtenstein died in 1939 at age 95.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1980s the Swiss Army fired off shells during an exercise and mistakenly burned a patch of forest inside Liechtenstein. The incident was said to have been resolved "over a case of white wine".<sup id="cite_ref-Letzing_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Letzing-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2007, a 170-man Swiss infantry unit got lost during a training exercise and inadvertently crossed 1.5&nbsp;km (0.9 miles) into Liechtenstein. The accidental invasion ended when the unit realized their mistake and turned back.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The Swiss Army later informed Liechtenstein of the incursion and offered official apologies,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> to which an internal ministry spokesperson responded, "No problem, these things happen."<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 7 April 2014, it was reported that the bank chief, Jürgen Frick, of the Bank Frick &amp; Co. based in Balzers was shot and killed in a parking garage in <a href="/wiki/Balzers" title="Balzers">Balzers</a>. The suspect, Jürgen Hermann, was found to have committed suicide after the shooting of the bank chief. Hermann was said to have been feuding with the bank for several years before the shooting took place. Hermann also called himself the "Robin Hood of Liechtenstein" on a website he was on. Hermann was also a former fund manager.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Liechtenstein signed the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liechtenstein&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
